AUTHOR: The Futurist
AUTHOR EMAIL: kartik_gada@yahoo.com
TITLE: Nine Tantalizing Small Companies
STATUS: Draft
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: six-tantalizing
CATEGORY: Accelerating Change
CATEGORY: Biotechnology
CATEGORY: Computing
CATEGORY: Nanotechnology
CATEGORY: Science
CATEGORY: Technological Breakthroughs

UNIQUE URL: https://atom.singularity2050.com/2008/02/six-tantalizing.html 
DATE: 02/17/2008 01:36:00 AM
-----
BODY:
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">In scouring the startup universe for the companies and technologies that can reshape human society and create entirely new industries, one has to play the role of a prospective Venture Capitalist, yet not be constrained by the need for a financial exit 3-6 years hence.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">Therefore, I have assembled a list of nine small companies, each with technologies that have the potential to create trillion-dollar economic disruptions by 2020.&#160; Note that the emphasis is on the technologies rather than the companies themselves, as a startup requires much more than a revolutionary technology in order to prosper.&#160; Management skills, team synergy, and execution efficiency are all equally important.&#160; I predict that out of this list of nine companies, perhaps one or two will become titans, while the others will be acquired by larger companies for modest sums, enabling the technology to reach the market through the acquiring company.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">1) <a href="http://www.nanosolar.com/index.html">NanoSolar</a> : NanoSolar produces low-cost solar cells that are manufactured by a process analogous to &#39;printing&#39;.&#160; The company&#39;s technology was selected by Popular Mechanics as the <a href="http://www.popsci.com/popsci/flat/bown/2007/green/item_59.html">&#39;Innovation of the Year&#39;</a> for 2007, and Nanosolar&#39;s solar cells are significantly ahead of the <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/08/solar-energy-co.html">Solar Energy Cost Curve</a>.&#160; The flexible, thin nature of Nanosolar&#39;s cells may enable them to be quickly incorporated onto the surfaces of many types of commercial buildings.&#160; Nanosolar&#39;s first shipments have already occurred, and if we see several large deployments in the near future, this might just be the company that finally makes solar energy a mass-adopted consumer technology.&#160; Nanosolar itself calls this the <a href="http://www.nanosolar.com/technology.htm">&#39;third wave&#39; of solar power technology</a>.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">2) <a href="http://www.teslamotors.com/">Tesla Motors</a> : <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/12/the_tesla_roads.html">I wrote about Tesla Motors in late 2006</a>.&#160; Tesla produces fully electric cars that can consume as little as 1 cent of electricity per mile.&#160; They are about to deliver the first few hundred units of the $98,000 Tesla Roadster to customers, and while the Roadster is not a car that can be marketed to average consumers, Tesla intends to release a 4-door $50,000 sedan named &#39;WhiteStar&#39; in 2010, and a $30,000 sedan by 2013.&#160; The press coverage devoted to Tesla Motors has been impressive, but until the WhiteStar sedan successfully sells at least 10,000 units, Tesla will not have silenced critics who say the technology cannot be brought down to mass-market costs.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/02/18/aptera_4.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=800,height=317,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"><img alt="Aptera_4" border="0" height="126" src="https://futurist.typepad.com/techsector/images/2008/02/18/aptera_4.jpg" style="FLOAT: right; MARGIN: 0px 0px 5px 5px" title="Aptera_4" width="320" /></a>3) <a href="http://www.aptera.com/">Aptera Motors</a> : When I first wrote about Tesla Motors, it was before I had heard about Aptera Motors.&#160; While Tesla is aiming to produce a $30,000 sedan for 2013, Aptera already has an all-electric car due for late 2008 that is priced at just $27,000, while delivering the equivalent of between 200 and 330 mpg.&#160; The fact that the vehicle has just three wheels may reduce mainstream appeal to some degree, but the futuristic appearance of the car will attract others.&#160; Aptera Motors is a top candidate for winning the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_X-Prize">Automotive X-Prize</a> in 2010.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The simultaneous use of Nanosolar&#39;s solar panels with the all-electric cars from Tesla and Aptera may enable automotive driving to be powered by <em>solar</em> generated electricity for the average single-family household.&#160; The combination of these two technologies would be the &#39;killer ap&#39; of getting off of oil and onto fully renewable energy for cars.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">4) <a href="https://www.23andme.com/">23andMe</a> : This company gets some press due to the fact that co-founder Anne Wojcicki is married to Sergey Brin, even as Google has poured $3.9M into 23andMe.&#160; Aside from this, what 23andMe offers is an individual&#39;s personal genome for just $1000.&#160; What a personal genome provides is a profile of which health conditions the customer is more or less susceptible to, and thus enables the customer to provide this information to his physician, and make the preventive lifestyle adjustments well in advance.&#160; Proactive consumers will be able to extend their lifespans by systematically reducing their risks of ailments they are genetically predisposed to.&#160; As the service is a function of computational power, the price of a personal genome will, of course, drop, and might become an integral part of the average person&#39;s medical records, as well as an expense that insurance covers.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">5) <a href="http://www.desktopfactory.com/">Desktop Factory</a> : In 2008, Desktop Factory will begin to sell a $5000 device that functions as a 3-D printer, printing solid objects one layer at a time.&#160; A user can scan almost any object (including a hand, foot, or head) and reproduce a miniature model of it (up to 5 X 5 X 5 inches).&#160; The material used by the 3-D printer costs about $1 per cubic inch.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The $5000 printer is a successor to similar $100,000 devices used in mechanical engineering and manufacturing firms.&#160; Due to the <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/02/the_impact_of_c.html">Impact of Computing</a>, consumer-targeted devices costing under $1000 will be available no later than 2014.&#160; I envision an ecosystem where people invent their own objects (statuettes, toys, tools, etc.) and share the scanned templates of these objects on social networking sites like MySpace and Facebook.&#160; People can thus &#39;share&#39; actual objects over the Internet, through printing a downloaded template.&#160; The cost of the printing material will drop over time as well.&#160; A lot of fun is to be had, and expect an impressive array of brilliant ideas to come from people below the age of 16.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">6) <a href="http://www.zazzle.com/">Zazzle</a> : Welcome to the age of the instapreneur.&#160; Zazzle enables anyone to design their own consumer commodities like T-shirts, mugs, calendars, bumper stickers, etc. on demand.&#160; If you have an idea, you can produce it on Zazzle with no start-up costs, and no inventory risks.&#160; You profit even from the very first unit you sell, with no worries about breakeven thresholds.&#160; You can produce an infinite number of products, limited only by your imagination.&#160; At this point, those of you reading this are probably in the midst of an avalanche of ideas of products you would like to produce.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">While the bulk of Zazzle users today are would merely be vanity users who manage to sell under ten units of their creations, this new paradigm of low-cost customization will inevitably creep up to major industrial supply chains.&#160; Even more interesting, think about #5 on this list, Desktop Factory, combining with Zazzle&#39;s application, into an amazing transformation of the very economics of manufacturing and mass-production.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">7) <a href="http://www.a123systems.com/#/home/cordless">A123 Systems</a> : <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2008/03/the-future-of-b.html">Read here about how battery technology is finally set to advance after decades of stagnation</a>.&#160; A123 Systems is at the forefront of these advances, and has already received over $148 Million in private funding, as well <a href="http://www.technologyreview.com/read_article.aspx?ch=specialsections&amp;sc=batteries&amp;id=20570&amp;a">as an article from the prestigious MIT Technology Review</a>.&#160; <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2008/04/27/automobiles/27PLUGIN.html?_r=1&amp;ex=1367121600&amp;en=4b209f17f9b54dae&amp;ei=5088&amp;partner=rssnyt&amp;emc=rss&amp;oref=slogin">A123 is a supplier for GM&#39;s upcoming Volt, and has already has begun to sell a module to convert a Toyota Prius into a plug-in hybrid</a>.&#160; For choices beyond those offered by the #2 and #3 companies on this list, A123 Systems is poised to enable the creation of many new electric or plug-in hybrid vehicles, greatly increasing the the choices available to consumers seeking the equivalent of more than 50 mpg.&#160; A123 may just become the Intel of batteries.&#160; Combine A123&#39;s batteries with Nanosolar&#39;s cells, and the possibilities become even more interesting.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">8) <a href="http://luxim.com/">Luxim</a> : Brightness of light is measured in Lumens, not Watts, which is a measure of power consumption.&#160; <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/09/the_imminent_re.html">Consumers are learning that CFL and LED bulbs offer the same Lumens with just a fifth or a tenth of the Watts consumed by a traditional incandescent bulb</a>, and billions of tons of coal are already being saved by the adoption of CFLs and LEDs.&#160; Luxim, however, aims to take this even further.&#160; Luxim makes tiny bulbs that deliver 8 times as many Lumens per Watt as incandescent bulbs.&#160; The bulbs are too expensive for home use, but are already going into projection TVs.&#160; With $61 Million in funding to date, Luxim&#39;s main hurdle will be to reduce the cost of their products enough to penetrate the vast home and office lighting market, which consumes tens of billions of bulbs each year.&#160; &#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">9) <a href="http://ugobe.com/">Ugobe</a> : Ugobe sells a robotic dinosaur toy known as the Pleo.&#160; A mere toy, especially a $350 toy, would not normally be on a list of technologies that promise to crease the fabric of human society.&#160; However, a closer look at the Pleo reveals many impressive increments in the march to make inexpensive robots more lifelike.&#160; The skin of the Pleo covers the joints, the Pleo has more advanced &#39;learning&#39; abilities than $2500 robots from a few years ago, and the Pleo even cries when tortured, to the extent that it is difficult to watch this.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The reason Ugobe is on this list is that I am curious to see what is the next product on their roadmap, so that I can gauge how quickly the technology is advancing.&#160; The next logical step would be an artificial mammal of some sort, with greater intelligence and realistic fur.&#160; The successful creation of this generation of robot would provide the datapoints to enable us to project the approximate arrival of future humanoid robots, for better or for worse.&#160; Another company may leapfrog Ugobe in the meantime, but they are currently at the forefront of the race to create low-priced robotic toys.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">This concludes the list of nine companies that each could greatly alter our lives within the next several years.&#160; Of these nine, at least three, Nanosolar, Tesla Motors, and 23andMe, have Google or Google&#39;s founders as investors.&#160; The next 24 months have important milestones for each of these companies to cross (by which time I might have a new list of new companies).&#160; For those that clear their respective near-term bars, there might just be a chance of attaining the dizzy heights that Google, Microsoft, or Intel has. </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">Related :</span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/02/the_impact_of_c.html">The Impact of Computing</a></span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/05/a_future_timeli.html">A Future Timeline for Automobiles</a></span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/02/a_future_timeli.html">A Future Timeline for Energy</a></span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/09/the_imminent_re.html">The Imminent Revolution in Lighting</a></span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2008/03/the-future-of-b.html">Batteries Set to Advance, Finally</a></span></p>

AUTHOR: The Futurist

TITLE: US Recession Began in December 2007
STATUS: Draft
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: us-recession-be
CATEGORY: Economics

UNIQUE URL: https://atom.singularity2050.com/2008/02/us-recession-be.html 
DATE: 02/05/2008 04:09:30 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">The US government usually declares a recession only several months after it has begun.&nbsp; I find the <a href="http://businesscycle.com/">Economic Cycle Research Institute</a> to be a vastly more reliable source of leading indicators.&nbsp; While the ECRI has still not declared a recession as 'unavoidable', the economic data of the last week tells me that it is, indeed, not just unavoidable at this point, but that it actually began in December 2007.&nbsp; It is far too late for any 'stimulus' to prevent a recession, nor will the EU manage to avoid hardship of its own</span><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">When <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/04/the_housing_bub.html">I identified the pervasive nature of the Housing Bubble way back on April 13, 2006</a>, I stated that housing may do poorly in inflation-adjusted terms even for the next 20 years (until 2026).&nbsp; Few were convinced then, now only somewhat more are.&nbsp; But supporting data for my prediction of the housing bubble being an event of generational duration is accumulating steadily.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Furthermore, when the US economy was not at any risk of recession on November 4, 2006, <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/11/the_us_economy_.html">I wrote an extended piece to refute the broken clocks who always insist the US is on the brink of collapse</a>.&nbsp; I declared that if recession does not happen by the end of 2007, then the housing bubble will no longer be a cause of recession, due to the housing correction being lengthy (hence digestible) rather than sharp.&nbsp; As the recession began in December 2007, we missed passing into the safety zone by just a hair.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">As the question of recession is now in the past, the next question is when a recovery may take place.&nbsp; The drop in economic conditions between October and January was so steep, and the Federal Reserve's reduction in rates in January, while belated, was so large in magnitude, that GDP recovery may arrive as soon as Q4.&nbsp; But I am not making a prediction on recovery timing yet. &nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2008/02/recession-began.html">Crossposted on The Futurist</a>.</span></p>

AUTHOR: The Futurist
AUTHOR EMAIL: kartik_gada@yahoo.com
TITLE: World Broadband Lines and Average Speeds
STATUS: Draft
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: world-broadband
CATEGORY: Accelerating Change
CATEGORY: Computing

UNIQUE URL: https://atom.singularity2050.com/2008/01/world-broadband.html 
DATE: 01/28/2008 01:17:24 AM
-----
BODY:
<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">World Broadband Lines in active use will reach 350 Million in 2008, and rise to 470 Million by 2010.&nbsp; Of equal significance, the <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/02/the_impact_of_c.html">Impact of Computing</a> ensures that the cost of network bandwidth continues to drop exponentially, and thus the average speed of each Broadband line is also increasing by as much as 30% a year.</span></p>

<p><a onclick="window.open(this.href, '_blank', 'width=646,height=481,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false" href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/26/bb_2.jpg"></a><a onclick="window.open(this.href, '_blank', 'width=644,height=481,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false" href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/26/bb_3.jpg"></a><a onclick="window.open(this.href, '_blank', 'width=644,height=481,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false" href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/28/bb.jpg"><img title="Bb" height="481" alt="Bb" src="https://futurist.typepad.com/techsector/images/2008/01/28/bb.jpg" width="644" border="0" /></a> </p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">As both the number and the average speed of lines are increasing simultaneously, this combined growth enables continued Internet evolution to occur much faster than most observers are expecting.&nbsp; </span><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/01/why_do_the_bigg.html">Technological changes often take observers by surprise</a> because they are fixated on just one advancing trend, while failing to notice another trend on a rapid collision course with the first.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Web 2.0 emerged a mere half-decade after the Internet bust (2000-02) due to the simultaneous combination of greater Internet connection speeds <em>and</em> wider Broadband penetration, leading to a greater number of people <em>each</em> spending more time online.&nbsp; The total aggregate person-hours spent on the Internet grew dramatically, enabling new business models to sustainably exist.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Thus, early in the next decade, the greater number of Broadband users, each with access to much higher speeds than today, will create an ecosystem that can sustain new Internet business models that may seem premature today.&nbsp; This will eventually be defined as 'Web 3.0', which could include technologies known today under the term of <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/06/the_semantic_we.html">'Semantic Web'</a>.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Be watchful of the companies that could become to Web 3.0 what YouTube, MySpace, Facebook, Wikipedia, etc. were to Web 2.0.&nbsp; </span></p>

TITLE: TechSector's Stock Portfolio for 2007 - RESULTS
STATUS: Draft
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: techsectors-sto
CATEGORY: Accelerating Change
CATEGORY: Economics
CATEGORY: Stock Picks
CATEGORY: Technological Breakthroughs

UNIQUE URL: https://atom.singularity2050.com/2008/01/techsectors-sto.html 
DATE: 01/16/2008 06:43:45 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/01/the_futurists_s.html">On January 23, 2007 on The Futurist, I created an investment portfolio to be frozen at that time</a>, and evaluated on December 31, 2007 against the benchmark of the S&amp;P500 index.&#160; The portfolio incorporated principles, economic trends, and technologies discussed in other articles here on The Futurist.&#160; Dividends were reinvested, and so the price paid reflects dividend-adjusted cost-basis.&#160; Yahoo and Google Finance do tend to miss recording some dividends, so one must go to a more reliable site like Morningstar to account for the exact dividends.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">So how did the portfolio do?&#160; I achieved a return of <strong><span style="COLOR: #336600">13.3%</span></strong>, vs. just <strong><span style="COLOR: #ff3300">4.3%</span></strong> for the S&amp;P500, from January 23 to December 31.&#160; Most fund managers are unable to beat the S&amp;P500 index despite the advanced tools at their disposal.&#160; The fraction of those that can beat the index by a margin 9.0 percentage points is even more exclusive, putting this portfolio in the top 10% of all mutual fund results for this period.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/12/2007stock_3.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/12/2007stock_4.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/12/2007stock_5.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/12/2007stock_6.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/16/2007stock.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/16/2007stock_2.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/16/2007stock_4.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=752,height=192,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.shared/image.html?/photos/uncategorized/2008/01/17/2007stock_3.jpg" onclick="window.open(this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=748,height=188,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39;); return false"></a><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/.a/6a00d83452455969e2010534d2933a970b-pi" style="DISPLAY: inline"><img alt="2007Port" class="at-xid-6a00d83452455969e2010534d2933a970b" src="https://futurist.typepad.com/.a/6a00d83452455969e2010534d2933a970b-550wi" style="WIDTH: 550px" /></a> &#160;</span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">As always, weightage matters just as much as stock-picking.&#160; The first two securities, amounting to 50% of my portfolio, were a total disaster.&#160; In fact, when I first created the portfolio, <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/01/the_futurists_s.html">I listed FXI as a security that was strongly considered but left out</a>.&#160; FXI returned an eye-popping 83% over the same period, so if I had included FXI instead of ICF, the portfolio&#39;s total return would have exceeded 25%.&#160; But it was not included, so &#39;what ifs&#39; do not count.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The India Investment Fund (IIF) was a star, more than compensating for the failure of the first two securities.&#160; But the real home runs came from the video game stocks.&#160; Three of the four outperformed the S&amp;P500, and two of those, Activision and GameStop, surged into the stratosphere.&#160; <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/04/the_next_big_th_2.html">My selection and detailed analysis of this sector way back on April 17, 2006</a> yielded a spectacular payoff.&#160; As a quartet, these 4 gaming stocks returned a combined 49% over this period.&#160; </span></p>
<p><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">So there you have it.&#160; Futurism is not impossible after all.&#160; <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2007/11/the-futurists-s.html">I have already started my 2008 portfolio, and we shall see how that goes on December 21, 2008</a>.&#160; The same principles covered in the articles below, are being applied.&#160; Let us see if the success can be repeated or exceeded.&#160; </span></p>
<p><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/04/the_next_big_th.html"><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The Next Big Thing in Entertainment, Part I</span></a><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">, </span><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/04/the_next_big_th_1.html"><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">Part 2</span></a><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">, and especially </span><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/04/the_next_big_th_2.html"><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">Part 3</span></a></p>
<p><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/12/what_determines.html"><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The Culture of Success</span></a><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em"> and </span><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/07/stock_market_ca.html"><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">Stock Market Capitalization in Developing Countries</span></a></p>
<p><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/02/the_stock_marke.html"><span style="FONT-SIZE: 1.2em">The Stock Market is Exponentially Accelerating too</span></a></p>

AUTHOR: The Futurist
AUTHOR EMAIL: kartik_gada@yahoo.com
TITLE: 2007 Technology Breakthrough Roundup
STATUS: Draft
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 1
BASENAME: now-we-arrive-a
CATEGORY: Accelerating Change
CATEGORY: Technological Breakthroughs

UNIQUE URL: https://atom.singularity2050.com/2008/01/now-we-arrive-a.html 
DATE: 01/16/2008 06:29:34 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">One year ago on The Futurist, <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/12/2006_technology.html">I posted a roundup of 2006 technology breakthroughs</a> from MIT Technology Review.&nbsp; Of the breakthroughs listed at that time, displays, plug-in hybrids, and solar cells showed impressive progress over the subsequent 12 months.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Now, we arrive at the 2007 list, which has expanded from four categories last year to five this time.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://www.technologyreview.com/Infotech/19986/">The Year in Software</a> </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://www.techreview.com/Infotech/19976/?a=f">The Year in Hardware</a> : Gadgetmania</span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://www.techreview.com/Energy/19981/">The Year in Energy</a> : Solar power inches closer.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://www.techreview.com/Biotech/19982/">The Year in Biotechnology</a> : Stem cell research methods that no longer need embryos.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://www.technologyreview.com/Nanotech/19983/">The Year in Nanotechnology</a> : Stanford University research into nanowires that dramatically increase battery capacity is the most promising breakthrough of 2007, in any discipline.&nbsp; Think 30-hour laptop batteries.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Most of the innovations in the articles above are in the laboratory phase, which means that about half will never progress enough to make it to market, and those that do will take 5 to 15 years to directly affect the lives of average people (remember that the laboratory-to-market transition period itself continues to shorten in most fields).&nbsp; But each one of these breakthroughs has world-changing potential, and that there are so many fields advancing simultaneously guarantees a massive new wave of improvement to human lives.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">This scorching <em>pace</em> of innovation is entirely predictable, however.&nbsp; To internalize the true rate of technological progress, one merely needs to appreciate :</span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">The <a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/04/mili_micro_nano.html">Milli, Micro, Nano, Pico curves</a></span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/02/the_impact_of_c.html">The Impact of Computing</a></span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;"><a href="http://futurist.typepad.com/my_weblog/2006/12/are_you_acceler.html">The Accelerating Rate of Change</a></span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">We are fortunate to live in an age when a single calendar year will invariably yield multiple technological breakthroughs, the details of which are easily accessible to laypeople.&nbsp; In the 18th century, entire decades would pass without any observable technological improvements, and people knew that their children would experience a lifestyle identical to their own.&nbsp; Today, we know with certainty that our lives in 2008 will have slight but distinct and numerous improvements in technological usage over 2007, just as 2007 was an improvement over 2006.&nbsp; </span></p>

<p><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">Into the Future we continue, where 2008 awaits..</span></p>
